1. e4 { Notes by Blackburne. } 1... e5 2. Nf3 Nc6 3. Bc4 { Italian game is on the board. } 3... Bc5 { This is the \'Giuoco Piano\' variation of the Italian game. } (3... Nf6 { Nf6 leads to \'Fried Liver Attack\'. } 4. Ng5 d5 5. exd5 Na5 6. Bb5+ c6 7. dxc6 bxc6 8. Qf3 Be7 9. Bxc6+ Nxc6 10. Qxc6+ Bd7 11. Qf3 O-O 12. d3 { And the game continues. Black is down 2 pawns> But he has compensation in the form of lead in development. White has to rapidly develop his pieces and castle his King into safety. }) 4. O-O { c3 is the move I would recommend. But White chooses to castle in the game. } 4... Nf6 5. d3 d6 6. h3 { h3 takes away the g4 square from Black\'s Knight and especially light squared bishop. But it also creates a hook that Black can target. } 6... Ne7 { Black is transferring his Knight to g6. Typical knight maneuver we see in the Italian and Spanish games. } 7. Bg5 c6 { Black is preparing d5 at the opportune moment. He is not afraid of Bxf6 and ruining of his King side pawn structure. Because then the g file will open up giving Black attacking chances against the White King. Note that Black King has not committed himself to any side of the board yet. } 8. Be3 { White is playing with the same piece twice in the opening. Not a good move. } 8... Bb6 { Black does not want to allow Bxc5 and doubling up of his c pawns. If Bxb6, then axb6 and Black opens up the a file for his Rook, bringing a pawn toward the center. } 9. Nc3 Ng6 { Knight landed on g6 as planned. } 10. Qd2 { White develops his Queen, connecting his Rooks. } 10... Be6 { Black offers a trade of light-squared Bishops. Bxe6 will double up Black\'s pawns on the e file. But the pawn on e6 will control key squares on the 5th rank, namely d5 and f5, preventing Black pieces from landing on those squares. Also the f file will open up which will give Black attacking chances after castling. } 11. Bb3 { White does not capture the Black\'s light-squared Bishop on e6 for the reasons explained above. \"To take is a mistake, unless it gives you an advantage!\" } 11... O-O 12. Rad1 { White develops his a Rook on d1. He intends to push d4. } 12... Qd7 { Black develops his Queen, connecting his Rooks. He formed a Queen and Bishop battery that eyeballs h3, the hook White created. } 13. Nh2 { White is preparing f4. } 13... Bxh3 { Here comes the Bishop sacrifice. Black wants to bring his Queen to the White King side and checkmate the White King using his Queen and 2 Knights. } 14. Bxb6 Bxg2 { Black is not in a hurry to capture axb6. First he captures the g2 pawn in front of White King, attacking White Rook on f1. He was going to sacrifice his light-squared Bishop anyway. } 15. Kxg2 Nf4+ 16. Kh1 axb6 { Now it\'s time to capture the Bishop on b6. } 17. f3 { White wants to protect his 2nd rank with his Queen and Rooks. He wants to be able to transfer his Queen to the King side to help out with the defense of his King, which is exposed. But that\'s too slow a move. White had to play Ne2 instead, trying to eliminate Black\'s very strong Knight on f4. } 17... N6h5 { Knight intends to jump to g3 forking White King and the Rook on f1. } 18. Rf2 { This does not stop Ng3+ } 18... Ng3+ 19. Kg1 Qh3 20. d4?? { That\'s a blunder. The only defense Black had was Rg2. But Black would still have the upper hand. Now mate is unavoidable. } 20... Qg2+ 21. Rxg2 Nh3# { 0-1 Black wins by checkmate. } 0-1
